	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en"><i>Dragon Ball</i></h1>

<p><i><b>Dragon Ball</b></i><span style="font-weight: normal"> (<a href="/wiki/Japanese_language" title="Japanese language">Japanese</a>: <span lang="ja">ドラゴンボール</span>, <a href="/wiki/Hepburn_romanization" title="Hepburn romanization">Hepburn</a>: <i lang="ja-Latn" title="Hepburn transliteration">Doragon Bōru</i>)</span> is a Japanese <a href="/wiki/Media_franchise" class="mw-redirect" title="Media franchise">media franchise</a> created by <a href="/wiki/Akira_Toriyama" title="Akira Toriyama">Akira Toriyama</a> in 1984. The <a href="/wiki/Dragon_Ball_(manga)" title="Dragon Ball (manga)">initial manga</a>, written and illustrated by Toriyama, was serialized in <i><a href="/wiki/Weekly_Sh%C5%8Dnen_Jump" title="Weekly Shōnen Jump">Weekly Shōnen Jump</a></i> from 1984 to 1995, with the 519 individual chapters collected into 42 <i><a href="/wiki/Tank%C5%8Dbon" title="Tankōbon">tankōbon</a></i> volumes by its publisher <a href="/wiki/Shueisha" title="Shueisha">Shueisha</a>. <i>Dragon Ball</i> was initially inspired by the classical Chinese novel <i><a href="/wiki/Journey_to_the_West" title="Journey to the West">Journey to the West</a></i>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_martial_arts_films" class="mw-redirect" title="Hong Kong martial arts films">Hong Kong martial arts films</a>. The series follows the adventures of the protagonist, <a href="/wiki/Goku" title="Goku">Son Goku</a>, from his childhood through adulthood as he trains in martial arts. He spends his childhood far from civilization until he meets a teen girl named <a href="/wiki/Bulma" title="Bulma">Bulma</a>, who encourages him to join her quest in exploring the world in search of the seven orbs known as the Dragon Balls, which summon a wish-granting dragon when gathered. Along his journey, Goku makes several other friends, becomes a family man, discovers his alien heritage, and battles a wide variety of villains, many of whom also seek the Dragon Balls.
</p><p>Toriyama's <a href="/wiki/Manga" title="Manga">manga</a> was adapted and divided into two <a href="/wiki/Anime" title="Anime">anime</a> series produced by <a href="/wiki/Toei_Animation" title="Toei Animation">Toei Animation</a>: <i><a href="/wiki/Dragon_Ball_(TV_series)" title="Dragon Ball (TV series)">Dragon Ball</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Dragon_Ball_Z" title="Dragon Ball Z">Dragon Ball Z</a></i>, which together were broadcast in Japan from 1986 to 1996. Additionally, the studio has developed <a href="/wiki/List_of_Dragon_Ball_films" title="List of Dragon Ball films">20 animated feature films</a> and three television specials, as well as two anime sequel series titled <i><a href="/wiki/Dragon_Ball_GT" title="Dragon Ball GT">Dragon Ball GT</a></i> (1996–1997) and <i><a href="/wiki/Dragon_Ball_Super" title="Dragon Ball Super">Dragon Ball Super</a></i> (2015–2018). From 2009 to 2015, a revised version of <i>Dragon Ball Z</i> aired in Japan under the title <i>Dragon Ball Kai</i>, as a recut that follows the manga's story more faithfully by removing most of the material featured exclusively in the anime. Several companies have developed various types of merchandising based on the series leading to a large media franchise that includes films, both animated and live-action, collectible trading card games, numerous action figures, along with <a href="/wiki/List_of_Dragon_Ball_soundtracks" title="List of Dragon Ball soundtracks">several collections of soundtracks</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Dragon_Ball_video_games" title="List of Dragon Ball video games">numerous video games</a>. <i>Dragon Ball</i> is one of the top twenty <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_media_franchises" title="List of highest-grossing media franchises">highest-grossing media franchises of all time</a>, having generated an estimated <span style="white-space: nowrap">$30 billion</span> in total franchise revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-Legend144_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Legend144-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since its release, <i>Dragon Ball</i> has become one of the most successful manga and anime series of all time, with the manga sold in over 40<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>countries and the anime broadcast in more than 80<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>countries. The manga's 42 collected <i>tankōbon</i> volumes have sold over 160<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million copies in Japan, and are estimated to have sold more than 250–300 million copies worldwide, making it the second <a href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_manga" title="List of best-selling manga">best-selling manga series</a> in history, behind only <i><a href="/wiki/One_Piece" title="One Piece">One Piece</a></i>. Reviewers have praised the art, characterization, and humour of the story. It is widely regarded as one of the greatest and most influential manga series ever made, with many <a href="/wiki/Mangaka" title="Mangaka">manga artists</a> citing <i>Dragon Ball</i> as a source of inspiration for their own now popular works. The anime, particularly <i>Dragon Ball Z</i>, is also highly popular across the world and is considered one of the most influential in boosting the popularity of Japanese animation in Western culture. It has had a considerable impact on global <a href="/wiki/Popular_culture" title="Popular culture">popular culture</a>, referenced by and inspiring numerous artists, athletes, celebrities, filmmakers, musicians and writers across the world.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Setting">Setting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dragon_Ball&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Setting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The Dragon Ball story takes place on Earth where Goku goes on adventures to find the Dragon Balls, as well as aspiring to become a great fighter, and compete in multiple martial arts tournaments. Goku later stops the evil Red Ribbon Army, then 3 years later, thwarts the Grand Demon King Piccolo's plans for world conquest, afterwards he and his friends protect the Earth from the Saiyan invasion. The setting also goes to Planet Namek later on in the series for Bulma, Gohan, and Kuririn to revive Goku's fallen friends from the Saiyan's attack, where they encounter Vegeta's higher ups, as well as the cosmic emperor, Freeza.
</p><p>The <i>Dragon Ball</i> franchise is set in a <a href="/wiki/Multiverse" title="Multiverse">multiverse</a><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> composed of twelve<sup id="cite_ref-Multiverse_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Multiverse-3">&#91;N 1&#93;</a></sup> numbered universes, each ruled by a number of benevolent and malevolent deities, respectively called Supreme Kais and Gods of Destruction. Almost all of the <i>Dragon Ball</i> series, except for parts of <i>Dragon Ball Super</i>, takes place in Universe 7. Years in the timeline are called "Ages", with most of the story occurring between Age 749 and Age 790.
</p><p>Universe 7 contains several planets, including a fictionalized Earth, where humans reside, and Planet Vegeta, the home world of the Saiyans, a powerful and destructive race. Many other races also inhabit Universe 7, including Angels, Demons, Androids, Tuffles and Namekians. Humans are among the weakest races in the universe. The protagonist Goku is raised as a human on Earth but finds out that he is actually a Saiyan from Planet Vegeta.
</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/Dr._Slump" title="Dr. Slump">Dr. Slump</a></i>, an earlier manga series by Akira Toriyama, is set in the same multiverse.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Production">Production</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dragon_Ball&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Production">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Dragon_Ball_characters" title="List of Dragon Ball characters">List of Dragon Ball characters</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dragon_Ball_(manga)#Production" title="Dragon Ball (manga)">Dragon Ball (manga) §&#160;Production</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Akira_Toriyama.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Akira_Toriyama.jpg/170px-Akira_Toriyama.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="272" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/04/Akira_Toriyama.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="254" data-file-height="407" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Akira_Toriyama.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Akira_Toriyama" title="Akira Toriyama">Akira Toriyama</a>, the creator of <i>Dragon Ball</i></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Akira_Toriyama" title="Akira Toriyama">Akira Toriyama</a> was a fan of <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_martial_arts_films" class="mw-redirect" title="Hong Kong martial arts films">Hong Kong martial arts films</a>, particularly <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Lee" title="Bruce Lee">Bruce Lee</a> films such as <i><a href="/wiki/Enter_the_Dragon" title="Enter the Dragon">Enter the Dragon</a></i> (1973) and <a href="/wiki/Jackie_Chan" title="Jackie Chan">Jackie Chan</a> films such as <i><a href="/wiki/Drunken_Master" title="Drunken Master">Drunken Master</a></i> (1978), and wanted to create a manga inspired by <a href="/wiki/Martial_arts_films" class="mw-redirect" title="Martial arts films">martial arts films</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Guide_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guide-4">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> This led to Toriyama creating the 1983 <a href="/wiki/One-shot_(comics)" title="One-shot (comics)">one-shot</a> manga <i>Dragon Boy</i>, which he later redeveloped into <i>Dragon Ball</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-AnimeEncyc_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AnimeEncyc-7">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Toriyama loosely modeled the plot and characters of <i>Dragon Ball</i> on the <a href="/wiki/Classic_Chinese_Novels" title="Classic Chinese Novels">classic Chinese novel</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Journey_to_the_West" title="Journey to the West">Journey to the West</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-Manga_Design_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Manga_Design-8">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AnimeEncyc_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AnimeEncyc-7">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> with Goku being <a href="/wiki/Sun_Wukong" class="mw-redirect" title="Sun Wukong">Sun Wukong</a> ("Son Goku" in Japanese), Bulma as <a href="/wiki/Tang_Sanzang" title="Tang Sanzang">Tang Sanzang</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_Dragon_Ball_characters#Oolong" title="List of Dragon Ball characters">Oolong</a> as <a href="/wiki/Zhu_Bajie" title="Zhu Bajie">Zhu Bajie</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Yamcha" title="Yamcha">Yamcha</a> being <a href="/wiki/Sha_Wujing" title="Sha Wujing">Sha Wujing</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Story_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Story-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Toriyama wanted to create a story with the basic theme of <i>Journey to the West</i>, but with "a little <a href="/wiki/Kung_fu" class="mw-redirect" title="Kung fu">kung fu</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-TenkaDen_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TenkaDen-10">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> The title <i>Dragon Ball</i> was inspired by <i>Enter the Dragon</i> and later <a href="/wiki/Bruceploitation" title="Bruceploitation">Bruceploitation</a> knockoff <a href="/wiki/Kung_fu_films" class="mw-redirect" title="Kung fu films">kung fu films</a> which frequently had the word "Dragon" in the title,<sup id="cite_ref-Guide_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guide-4">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> and the fighting scenes were influenced by Jackie Chan movies.<sup id="cite_ref-Illustrations_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Illustrations-11">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Story_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Story-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Since it was serialized in a <a href="/wiki/Sh%C5%8Dnen_manga" title="Shōnen manga">shōnen</a> <a href="/wiki/Manga_magazine" class="mw-redirect" title="Manga magazine">manga magazine</a>, he added the idea of the Dragon Balls to give it a game-like activity of gathering something, without thinking of what the characters would wish for.<sup id="cite_ref-TenkaDen_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TenkaDen-10">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> His concept of the Dragon Balls was inspired by the epic <a href="/wiki/Japanese_novel" class="mw-redirect" title="Japanese novel">Japanese novel</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Nans%C5%8D_Satomi_Hakkenden" title="Nansō Satomi Hakkenden">Nansō Satomi Hakkenden</a></i> (1814–1842), which involves the heroes collecting eight <a href="/wiki/Buddhist" class="mw-redirect" title="Buddhist">Buddhist</a> <a href="/wiki/Prayer_beads" title="Prayer beads">prayer beads</a>, which Toriyama adapted into collecting seven Dragon Balls.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He originally thought it would last about a year or end once the Dragon Balls were collected.<sup id="cite_ref-Shenlong2_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shenlong2-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Toriyama stated that although the stories are purposefully easy to understand, he specifically aimed <i>Dragon Ball</i> at readers older than those of his previous serial <i><a href="/wiki/Dr._Slump" title="Dr. Slump">Dr. Slump</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> He also wanted to break from the Western influences common in <i>Dr. Slump</i>, deliberately going for Chinese scenery, referencing Chinese buildings and photographs of <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> his wife had bought.<sup id="cite_ref-World_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Toriyama wanted to set <i>Dragon Ball</i> in a fictional world largely based on <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a>, taking inspiration from several <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Asia" title="Culture of Asia">Asian cultures</a> including <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Japan" title="Culture of Japan">Japanese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chinese_culture" title="Chinese culture">Chinese</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South Asian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arabic_culture" title="Arabic culture">Arabic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_culture" class="mw-redirect" title="Indonesian culture">Indonesian cultures</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> The island where the Tenkaichi Budōkai<span style="font-weight: normal"> (<span lang="ja" title="Japanese language text">天下一武道会</span>, lit. "Strongest Under the Heavens Martial Arts Tournament")</span> is held is modeled after <a href="/wiki/Bali" title="Bali">Bali</a> (in <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>), which he, his wife and assistant visited in mid-1985, and for the area around <a href="/wiki/Babidi" class="mw-redirect" title="Babidi">Bobbidi</a>'s spaceship he consulted photos of <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-World_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Toriyama was also inspired by the <a href="/wiki/Jinn" title="Jinn">jinn</a> (genies) from <i><a href="/wiki/The_Arabian_Nights" class="mw-redirect" title="The Arabian Nights">The Arabian Nights</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wiki_DragonBall_Earth.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/05/Wiki_DragonBall_Earth.png/220px-Wiki_DragonBall_Earth.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="168" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/05/Wiki_DragonBall_Earth.png/330px-Wiki_DragonBall_Earth.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/05/Wiki_DragonBall_Earth.png/440px-Wiki_DragonBall_Earth.png 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="610" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wiki_DragonBall_Earth.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Earth of <i>Dragon Ball</i>, as published in <i>Daizenshuu 4: World Guide</i></div></div></div>
<p>During the early chapters of the manga Toriyama's editor, <a href="/wiki/Kazuhiko_Torishima" title="Kazuhiko Torishima">Kazuhiko Torishima</a>, commented that Goku looked rather plain, so to combat this he added several characters like <a href="/wiki/Master_Roshi" title="Master Roshi">Kame-Sen'nin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Krillin" title="Krillin">Kuririn</a>, and created the Tenkaichi Budōkai martial arts tournament to focus the storyline on fighting. It was when the first Tenkaichi Budōkai began that <i>Dragon Ball</i> truly became popular, having recalled the races and tournaments in <i>Dr. Slump</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Story_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Story-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Anticipating that readers would expect Goku to win the tournaments, Toriyama had him lose the first two while planning an eventual victory. He said that Muscle Tower in the Red Ribbon Army storyline was inspired by the video game <i><a href="/wiki/Kung-Fu_Master_(video_game)" title="Kung-Fu Master (video game)">Spartan X</a></i>, in which enemies tended to appear very fast. He then created <a href="/wiki/Piccolo_(Dragon_Ball)" title="Piccolo (Dragon Ball)">Piccolo Daimao</a> as a truly evil villain, and as a result called that arc the most interesting to draw.<sup id="cite_ref-Story_9-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Story-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Once Goku and company had become the strongest on Earth, they turned to extraterrestrial opponents including the Saiyans<span style="font-weight: normal"> (<span lang="ja" title="Japanese language text">サイヤ人</span>, <i lang="ja-Latn" title="Hepburn transliteration">Saiya-jin</i>)</span>; and Goku himself was <a href="/wiki/Retroactive_continuity" title="Retroactive continuity">retconned</a> from an Earthling to a Saiyan who was sent to Earth as a baby.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Frieza" title="Frieza">Freeza</a>, who forcibly took over planets to resell them, was created around the time of the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_asset_price_bubble" title="Japanese asset price bubble">Japanese economic bubble</a> and was inspired by <a href="/wiki/Real_estate" title="Real estate">real estate</a> <a href="/wiki/Speculation" title="Speculation">speculators</a>, whom Toriyama called the "worst kind of people."<sup id="cite_ref-Story_9-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Story-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Finding the escalating enemies difficult, he created the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Dragon_Ball_characters#Ginyu_Force" title="List of Dragon Ball characters">Ginyu Force</a> to add more balance to the series. When Toriyama created the Super Saiyan<span style="font-weight: normal"> (<span lang="ja" title="Japanese language text"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r963368435">.mw-parser-output ruby>rt,.mw-parser-output ruby>rtc{font-feature-settings:"ruby"1;font-size:85%}.mw-parser-output ruby.large{font-size:250%}.mw-parser-output ruby.large>rt,.mw-parser-output ruby.large>rtc{font-size:50%}</style><ruby><rb>超</rb><rp>&#32;(</rp><rt>スーパー</rt><rp>)</rp></ruby>サイヤ人</span>, <i lang="ja-Latn" title="Hepburn transliteration">Sūpā Saiya-jin</i>)</span> transformation during the Freeza arc, he was initially concerned that Goku's facial expressions as a Super Saiyan made him look like a villain, but decided it was acceptable since the transformation was brought about by anger.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Goku's Super Saiyan form has blonde hair because it was easier to draw for Toriyama's assistant (who spent a lot of time blacking in Goku's hair), and has piercing eyes based on Bruce Lee's paralyzing glare.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Toriyama added <a href="/wiki/Time_travel" title="Time travel">time travel</a> next during the <a href="/wiki/Cell_(Dragon_Ball)" title="Cell (Dragon Ball)">Cell</a> arc, but said he had a hard time with it, only thinking of what to do that week and having to discuss it with his second editor Yu Kondo.<sup id="cite_ref-Story_9-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Story-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> After Cell's death, Toriyama intended for <a href="/wiki/Gohan" title="Gohan">Gohan</a> to replace Goku as the series' <a href="/wiki/Protagonist" title="Protagonist">protagonist</a>, but felt the character was not suited for the role and changed his mind.<sup id="cite_ref-Story_9-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Story-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Going against the normal convention that the strongest characters should be the largest in terms of physical size, he designed many of <i>Dragon Ball</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> most powerful characters with small statures, including the protagonist, Goku.<sup id="cite_ref-SJ_interview_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SJ_interview-21">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Toriyama later explained that he had Goku grow up as a means to make drawing fight scenes easier, even though his first editor <a href="/wiki/Kazuhiko_Torishima" title="Kazuhiko Torishima">Kazuhiko Torishima</a> was initially against it because it was rare to have the main character of a manga series change drastically.<sup id="cite_ref-Chogashu_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chogashu-22">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> When including fights in the manga, Toriyama had the characters go to uninhabited locations to avoid difficulties in drawing residents and destroyed buildings.<sup id="cite_ref-World_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Toriyama said that he did not plan the details of the story, resulting in strange occurrences and discrepancies later in the series, including changing the colors of the characters mid-story and few characters having <a href="/wiki/Screentone" title="Screentone">screentone</a> because he found it difficult to use.<sup id="cite_ref-Illustrations_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Illustrations-11">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-TenkaDen_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TenkaDen-10">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Shenlong2_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shenlong2-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Since the completion of <i>Dragon Ball</i>, Toriyama has continued to add to its story, mostly background information on its universe, through guidebooks published by Shueisha.
</p><p>During the second half of the series, Toriyama has said that he had become more interested in coming up with the story than actually drawing it, and that the battles became more intense with him simplifying the lines.<sup id="cite_ref-Illustrations_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Illustrations-11">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> In 2013, he stated that because <i>Dragon Ball</i> is an action manga the most important aspect is the sense of speed, so he did not draw very elaborate, going so far as to suggest one could say that he was not interested in the art.<sup id="cite_ref-Chogashu_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chogashu-22">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> He also once said that his goal for the series was to tell an "unconventional and contradictory" story.<sup id="cite_ref-SJ_interview_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SJ_interview-21">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> In 2013, commenting on <i>Dragon Ball</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s global success, Toriyama said, "Frankly, I don't quite understand why it happened. While the manga was being serialized, the only thing I wanted as I kept drawing was to make Japanese boys happy.", "The role of my manga is to be a work of entertainment through and through. I dare say I don't care even if [my works] have left nothing behind, as long as they have entertained their readers."<sup id="cite_ref-AsahiInterview_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AsahiInterview-24">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Manga">Manga</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dragon_Ball&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Manga">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Dragon_Ball_(manga)" title="Dragon Ball (manga)">Dragon Ball (manga)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Weekly_Sh%C5%8Dnen_Jump_No._51_(Dec._1984)_is_the_first_appearance_of_Goku._Cover_art_by_Akira_Toriyama.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/24/Weekly_Sh%C5%8Dnen_Jump_No._51_%28Dec._1984%29_is_the_first_appearance_of_Goku._Cover_art_by_Akira_Toriyama.jpg/170px-Weekly_Sh%C5%8Dnen_Jump_No._51_%28Dec._1984%29_is_the_first_appearance_of_Goku._Cover_art_by_Akira_Toriyama.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="240" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/24/Weekly_Sh%C5%8Dnen_Jump_No._51_%28Dec._1984%29_is_the_first_appearance_of_Goku._Cover_art_by_Akira_Toriyama.jpg/255px-Weekly_Sh%C5%8Dnen_Jump_No._51_%28Dec._1984%29_is_the_first_appearance_of_Goku._Cover_art_by_Akira_Toriyama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/2/24/Weekly_Sh%C5%8Dnen_Jump_No._51_%28Dec._1984%29_is_the_first_appearance_of_Goku._Cover_art_by_Akira_Toriyama.jpg 2x" data-file-width="265" data-file-height="374" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Weekly_Sh%C5%8Dnen_Jump_No._51_(Dec._1984)_is_the_first_appearance_of_Goku._Cover_art_by_Akira_Toriyama.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Dragon Ball</i> debuted in <i>Weekly Shōnen Jump</i> No. 51, on December 3, 1984.</div></div></div>
<p>Written and illustrated by Akira Toriyama, <i>Dragon Ball</i> was serialized in the manga anthology <i><a href="/wiki/Weekly_Sh%C5%8Dnen_Jump" title="Weekly Shōnen Jump">Weekly Shōnen Jump</a></i> from December 3, 1984 to June 5, 1995,<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> when Toriyama grew exhausted and felt he needed a break from drawing. The 519 individual chapters were published into 42 <i><a href="/wiki/Tank%C5%8Dbon" title="Tankōbon">tankōbon</a></i> volumes by <a href="/wiki/Shueisha" title="Shueisha">Shueisha</a> from September 10, 1985 through August 4, 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-sold_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sold-27">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Shueisha_1_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shueisha_1-28">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ShueishaZ_26_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ShueishaZ_26-29">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Between December 4, 2002 and April 2, 2004, the chapters were re-released in a collection of 34 <i><a href="/wiki/Kanzenban" class="mw-redirect" title="Kanzenban">kanzenban</a></i> volumes, which included a slightly rewritten ending, new covers, and color artwork from its <i>Weekly Shōnen Jump</i> run.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> The February 2013 issue of <i><a href="/wiki/V_Jump" title="V Jump">V Jump</a></i>, which was released in December 2012, announced that parts of the manga will be fully colored and re-released in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-colorchozenshuu_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-colorchozenshuu-32">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Twenty volumes, beginning from chapter 195 and grouped by story arcs, were released between February 4, 2013 and July 4, 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Twelve volumes covering the first 194 chapters were published between January 4 and March 4, 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> A <i><a href="/wiki/S%C5%8Dsh%C5%ABhen" class="mw-redirect" title="Sōshūhen">sōshūhen</a></i> edition that aims to recreate the manga as it was originally serialized in <i>Weekly Shōnen Jump</i> with color pages, promotional text, and next chapter previews, was published in eighteen volumes between May 13, 2016 and January 13, 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Spin-offs">Spin-offs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dragon_Ball&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Spin-offs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Another manga penned by Ōishi, the three-chapter <i><a href="/wiki/Dragon_Ball:_Episode_of_Bardock" title="Dragon Ball: Episode of Bardock">Dragon Ball: Episode of Bardock</a></i> that revolves around <a href="/wiki/Burdock_(Dragon_Ball)" class="mw-redirect" title="Burdock (Dragon Ball)">Bardock</a>, Goku's father, was published in the monthly magazine <i><a href="/wiki/V_Jump" title="V Jump">V Jump</a></i> from August and October 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The final chapter of Toriyama's 2013 manga series <i><a href="/wiki/Jaco_the_Galactic_Patrolman" title="Jaco the Galactic Patrolman">Jaco the Galactic Patrolman</a></i> revealed that it is set before <i>Dragon Ball</i>, with several characters making appearances.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> <i>Jaco</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> collected volumes contain a bonus <i>Dragon Ball</i> chapter depicting Goku's mother.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2016, a spin-off manga titled <i>Dragon Ball Side Story: The Case of Being Reincarnated as Yamcha</i> began in Shueisha's <i>Shōnen Jump+</i> digital magazine. Written and illustrated by Dragon Garow Lee, it is about a high school boy who after an accident wakes up in the body of Yamcha in the <i>Dragon Ball</i> manga.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Crossovers">Crossovers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dragon_Ball&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Crossovers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Toriyama also created a short series, <i><a href="/wiki/Neko_Majin" title="Neko Majin">Neko Majin</a></i> (1999–2005), that became a self-parody of <i>Dragon Ball</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> In 2006, a <a href="/wiki/Fictional_crossover" class="mw-redirect" title="Fictional crossover">crossover</a> between <i><a href="/wiki/Kochira_Katsushika-ku_Kameari_K%C5%8Den-mae_Hashutsujo" title="Kochira Katsushika-ku Kameari Kōen-mae Hashutsujo">Kochira Katsushika-ku Kameari Kōen-mae Hashutsujo</a></i> (or <i>Kochikame</i>) and <i>Dragon Ball</i> by Toriyama and <i>Kochikame</i> author <a href="/wiki/Osamu_Akimoto" title="Osamu Akimoto">Osamu Akimoto</a> appeared in the <i>Super Kochikame</i><span style="font-weight: normal"> (<span lang="ja" title="Japanese language text">超こち亀</span>, <i lang="ja-Latn" title="Hepburn transliteration">Chō Kochikame</i>)</span> manga.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> That same year, Toriyama teamed up with <a href="/wiki/Eiichiro_Oda" title="Eiichiro Oda">Eiichiro Oda</a> to create a crossover chapter of <i>Dragon Ball</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/One_Piece" title="One Piece">One Piece</a></i> titled <i>Cross Epoch</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
