<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Dragon_Ball_(manga)#Reception" title="Dragon Ball (manga)">Dragon Ball (manga) §&#160;Reception</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Weekly_Sh%C5%8Dnen_Jump#Circulation_figures" title="Weekly Shōnen Jump">Weekly Shōnen Jump §&#160;Circulation figures</a></div>
<p><i>Dragon Ball</i> is one of the most popular manga series of all time, and it continues to enjoy high readership today. <i>Dragon Ball</i> is credited as one of the main reasons manga circulation was at its highest between the mid-1980s and mid-1990s.<sup id="cite_ref-IbarakiInterview_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IbarakiInterview-80">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-comipress-jump_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-comipress-jump-81">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> During <i>Dragon Ball</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s initial run in <i><a href="/wiki/Weekly_Sh%C5%8Dnen_Jump" title="Weekly Shōnen Jump">Weekly Shōnen Jump</a></i>, the <a href="/wiki/Manga_magazine" class="mw-redirect" title="Manga magazine">manga magazine</a> reached an average circulation of 6.53<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million weekly sales, the highest in its history.<sup id="cite_ref-IbarakiInterview_80-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IbarakiInterview-80">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-comipress-jump_81-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-comipress-jump-81">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-TimeMag_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TimeMag-82">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> During <i>Dragon Ball</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s serialisation between 1984 and 1995, <i>Weekly Shōnen Jump</i> magazine had a total circulation of over 2.9<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>billion copies,<sup id="cite_ref-exlight_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-exlight-83">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Circulation_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Circulation-84">&#91;g&#93;</a></sup> with those issues generating an estimated <span style="white-space: nowrap">¥554 billion</span> (<span style="white-space: nowrap">$6.9 billion</span>) in sales revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-Circulation_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Circulation-84">&#91;g&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i>Dragon Ball</i> also sold a record number of collected <i><a href="/wiki/Tank%C5%8Dbon" title="Tankōbon">tankōbon</a></i> volumes for its time. By 2000, more than 126<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million <i>tankōbon</i> copies had been sold in Japan alone.<sup id="cite_ref-LittleBoy_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LittleBoy-85">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> It sold over 150<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million copies in Japan by 2008, making it the <a href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_manga" title="List of best-selling manga">best-selling manga</a> ever at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> By 2012, its sales in Japan had grown to pass 156<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million, making it the second best-selling <i>Weekly Shōnen Jump</i> manga of all time, behind <i><a href="/wiki/One_Piece" title="One Piece">One Piece</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-156mil_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156mil-87">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> <i>Dragon Ball</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s <i>tankobon</i> volumes sold 159.5<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million copies in Japan by February 2014,<sup id="cite_ref-jump2014_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jump2014-88">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> and have sold over 160<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million copies in Japan as of 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-naver_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-naver-48">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The manga is similarly popular overseas, having been translated and released in over 40<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>countries worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> Estimates for the total number of <i>tankōbon</i> volumes sold worldwide range from more than 250<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million copies<sup id="cite_ref-naver_48-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-naver-48">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> to more than 300<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million copies,<sup id="cite_ref-sfchronicle_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sfchronicle-98">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Booker_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Booker-99">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-livedoor_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-livedoor-100">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sankei_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sankei-101">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-oricon-sales_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oricon-sales-102">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-comipress_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-comipress-103">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> not including unofficial pirated copies; when including pirated copies, an estimated total of over 400<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million official and unofficial copies have been sold worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-Pirate_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pirate-79">&#91;f&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-China_49-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-China-49">&#91;b&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Korea_50-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Korea-50">&#91;c&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>For the 10th anniversary of the <a href="/wiki/Japan_Media_Arts_Festival" title="Japan Media Arts Festival">Japan Media Arts Festival</a> in 2006, Japanese fans voted <i>Dragon Ball</i> the third greatest manga of all time.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> In a survey conducted by <a href="/wiki/Oricon" title="Oricon">Oricon</a> in 2007 among 1,000 people, Son Goku, the main character of the franchise, ranked first place as the "Strongest Manga Character of All Time."<sup id="cite_ref-oricon_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oricon-105">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> Goku's journey and his ever-growing strength resulted in the character winning "the admiration of young boys everywhere".<sup id="cite_ref-Manga_Design_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Manga_Design-8">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Manga artists, such as <i><a href="/wiki/One_Piece" title="One Piece">One Piece</a></i> creator <a href="/wiki/Eiichiro_Oda" title="Eiichiro Oda">Eiichiro Oda</a> and <i><a href="/wiki/Naruto" title="Naruto">Naruto</a></i> creator <a href="/wiki/Masashi_Kishimoto" title="Masashi Kishimoto">Masashi Kishimoto</a>, have stated that Goku inspired their series' main protagonists as well as series structure.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Manga critic <a href="/wiki/Jason_Thompson_(writer)" title="Jason Thompson (writer)">Jason Thompson</a> stated in 2011 that "<i>Dragon Ball</i> is by far the most influential shonen manga of the last 30 years, and today, almost every <i>Shonen Jump</i> artist lists it as one of their favorites and lifts from it in various ways."<sup id="cite_ref-ANNJT_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ANNJT-108">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> He says the series "turns from a gag/adventure manga to an nearly-pure fighting manga",<sup id="cite_ref-ANNJT_108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ANNJT-108">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> and its basic formula of "lots of martial arts, lots of training sequences, a few jokes" became the model for other <a href="/wiki/Sh%C5%8Dnen_manga" title="Shōnen manga">shōnen</a> series, such as <i>Naruto</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> Thompson also called Toriyama's art influential and cited it as a reason for the series' popularity.<sup id="cite_ref-ANNJT_108-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ANNJT-108">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> James S. Yadao, author of <i>The Rough Guide to Manga</i>, claims that the first several chapters of <i>Dragon Ball </i>"play out much like <i><a href="/wiki/Journey_to_the_West" title="Journey to the West">Saiyuki</a></i> with <i><a href="/wiki/Dr._Slump" title="Dr. Slump">Dr. Slump</a></i>-like humour built in" and that <i>Dr. Slump</i>, Toriyama's previous manga, has a clear early influence on the series.<sup id="cite_ref-Yadao116_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yadao116-110">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> He feels the series "established its unique identity" after the first occasion when Goku's group disbands and he trains under Kame-sen'nin, when the story develops "a far more action-packed, sinister tone" with "wilder" battles with aerial and spiritual elements and an increased death count, while humor still makes an occasional appearance.<sup id="cite_ref-Yadao116_110-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yadao116-110">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> Yadao claims that an art shift occurs when the characters "lose the rounded, innocent look that he established in <i>Dr. Slump</i> and gain sharper angles that leap off the page with their energy and intensity."<sup id="cite_ref-Yadao116117_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yadao116117-111">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/Animerica" title="Animerica">Animerica</a></i> felt the series had "worldwide appeal", using dramatic pacing and over-the-top martial arts action to "maintain tension levels and keep a crippler crossface hold on the audience's attention spans".<sup id="cite_ref-Animerica_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Animerica-112">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> In <i>Little Boy: The Art of Japan's Exploding Subculture</i>, Takashi Murakami commented that <i>Dragon Ball</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> "never-ending cyclical narrative moves forward plausibly, seamlessly, and with great finesse."<sup id="cite_ref-LittleBoy_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LittleBoy-85">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> Ridwan Khan from Animefringe.com commented that the manga had a "chubby" art style, but as the series continued the characters got more refined, leaner, and more muscular. Khan prefers the manga over the slow pacing of the anime counterparts.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> Allen Divers of <a href="/wiki/Anime_News_Network" title="Anime News Network">Anime News Network</a> praised the story and humor of the manga as being very good at conveying all of the characters' personalities. Divers also called <a href="/wiki/Viz_Media" title="Viz Media">Viz</a>'s translation one of the best of all the English editions of the series due to its faithfulness to the original Japanese.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> D. Aviva Rothschild of Rationalmagic.com remarked the first manga volume as "a superior humor title". They praised Goku's innocence and Bulma's insistence as one of the funniest parts of the series.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The content of the manga has been controversial in the United States. In November 1999, <a href="/wiki/Toys_%22R%22_Us" title="Toys &quot;R&quot; Us">Toys "R" Us</a> removed Viz's <i>Dragon Ball</i> from their stores nationwide when a <a href="/wiki/Dallas" title="Dallas">Dallas</a> parent complained the series had "borderline soft porn" after he bought them for his four-year-old son.<sup id="cite_ref-Maryland_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Maryland-116">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> Commenting on the issue, <a href="/wiki/Susan_J._Napier" title="Susan J. Napier">Susan J. Napier</a> explained it as a difference in culture.<sup id="cite_ref-Maryland_116-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Maryland-116">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> After the ban, Viz reluctantly began to censor the series to keep wide distribution.<sup id="cite_ref-censorship2_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-censorship2-117">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> However, in 2001, after releasing three volumes censored, Viz announced <i>Dragon Ball</i> would be uncensored and reprinted due to fan reactions.<sup id="cite_ref-censorship2_117-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-censorship2-117">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> In October 2009, <a href="/wiki/Wicomico_County_Public_Schools" title="Wicomico County Public Schools">Wicomico County Public Schools</a> in <a href="/wiki/Maryland" title="Maryland">Maryland</a> banned the <i>Dragon Ball</i> manga from their school district because it "depicts nudity, sexual contact between children and sexual innuendo among adults and children."<sup id="cite_ref-Maryland_116-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Maryland-116">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Anime">Anime</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dragon_Ball&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Anime">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Dragon_Ball_anime" title="List of Dragon Ball anime">List of Dragon Ball anime</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Main_installments">Main installments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dragon_Ball&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Main installments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>Dragon Ball</i> and <i>Dragon Ball Z</i> are adaptations of the original <i>Dragon Ball</i> manga, with various new material added in to make extra episodes so that Toriyama would have more time to write original chapters for them to adapt. <i>Dragon Ball Z Kai</i> is a version of the <i>Dragon Ball Z</i> that removes most of the episodes featuring content that was not part of the original manga. The sequel to the original manga is called <i>Dragon Ball Super</i>, and its story is based on a plot outline by Toriyama. Unlike previous anime series, <i>Super</i> is released in parallel to, and many times ahead of, the manga of the same name; despite being based on the same outline by Toriyama, there are many slight plot differences between the manga and the anime.
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Dragon_Ball"><i>Dragon Ball</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dragon_Ball&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Dragon Ball">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Dragon_Ball_(TV_series)" title="Dragon Ball (TV series)">Dragon Ball (TV series)</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Dragon_Ball_episodes" title="List of Dragon Ball episodes">List of Dragon Ball episodes</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Toei_Animation" title="Toei Animation">Toei Animation</a> produced an <a href="/wiki/Anime" title="Anime">anime</a> television series based on the first 194 manga chapters, also titled <i>Dragon Ball</i>. The series premiered in Japan on <a href="/wiki/Fuji_Television" class="mw-redirect" title="Fuji Television">Fuji Television</a> on February 26, 1986 and ran until April 19, 1989, lasting 153 episodes.<sup id="cite_ref-AnimeEncyc_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AnimeEncyc-7">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> It is broadcast in 81<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>countries worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-gamebiz_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gamebiz-118">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Dragon_Ball_Z"><i>Dragon Ball Z</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dragon_Ball&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Dragon Ball Z">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Dragon_Ball_Z" title="Dragon Ball Z">Dragon Ball Z</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Dragon_Ball_Z_episodes" title="List of Dragon Ball Z episodes">List of Dragon Ball Z episodes</a></div>
<p>Instead of continuing the anime as <i>Dragon Ball</i>, Toei Animation decided to carry on with their adaptation under a new name and asked Akira Toriyama to come up with the title. <i>Dragon Ball Z</i><span style="font-weight: normal"> (<span lang="ja" title="Japanese language text">ドラゴンボールZ(ゼット)</span>, <i lang="ja-Latn" title="Hepburn transliteration">Doragon Bōru Zetto</i>, commonly abbreviated as <i>DBZ</i>)</span> picks up five years after the first series left off and adapts the final 325 chapters of the manga. It premiered in Japan on Fuji Television on April 26, 1989, taking over its predecessor's time slot, and ran for 291 episodes until its conclusion on January 31, 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-AnimeEncyc_7-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AnimeEncyc-7">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Two television specials based on the <i>Z</i> series were aired on Fuji TV in Japan. The first, <i>The One True Final Battle ~The Z Warrior Who Challenged Frieza – Son Goku's Father~</i>, renamed <i><a href="/wiki/Dragon_Ball_Z:_Bardock_%E2%80%93_The_Father_of_Goku" title="Dragon Ball Z: Bardock – The Father of Goku">Bardock – The Father of Goku</a></i> by Funimation, was shown on October 17, 1990. The second special, <i>Defiance in the Face of Despair!! The Remaining Super-Warriors: Gohan and Trunks</i>, renamed <i><a href="/wiki/Dragon_Ball_Z:_The_History_of_Trunks" title="Dragon Ball Z: The History of Trunks">The History of Trunks</a></i> by Funimation, is based on a special chapter of the original manga and aired on February 24, 1993.
</p>
<ul><li><i><b>Dragon Ball Z Kai</b></i> (Remastered Director's Cut)</li></ul>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Dragon_Ball_Z_Kai_episodes" title="List of Dragon Ball Z Kai episodes">List of Dragon Ball Z Kai episodes</a></div>
<p>In February 2009, <i>Dragon Ball Z</i> celebrated its 20th anniversary, with Toei Animation announcing that it would broadcast a re-edited and remastered version under the name <i>Dragon Ball Kai</i><span style="font-weight: normal"> (<span lang="ja" title="Japanese language text">ドラゴンボール改</span>, <i lang="ja-Latn" title="Hepburn transliteration">Doragon Bōru Kai</i>, lit. "Dragon Ball Revised")</span>. The footage would be re-edited to follow the manga more closely, eliminating scenes and episodes which were not featured in the original manga, resulting in a more faithful adaptation, as well as in a faster-moving, and more focused story.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> The episodes were remastered for <a href="/wiki/High-definition_television" title="High-definition television">HDTV</a>, with rerecording of the vocal tracks by most of the original cast, and featuring updated opening and ending sequences. On April 5, 2009, the series premiered in Japan airing in Fuji TV.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> <i>Dragon Ball Z Kai</i> reduced the episode count to 159 episodes (167 episodes internationally), from the original footage of 291 episodes. Damaged frames were removed, resulting in some minor shots being remade from scratch in order to fix cropping, and others to address continuity issues.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> The majority of the international versions, including <a href="/wiki/Funimation" title="Funimation">Funimation Entertainment</a>'s English dub, are titled <i>Dragon Ball Z Kai</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Dragon_Ball_Super"><i>Dragon Ball Super</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dragon_Ball&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Dragon Ball Super">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Dragon_Ball_Super" title="Dragon Ball Super">Dragon Ball Super</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Dragon_Ball_Super_episodes" title="List of Dragon Ball Super episodes">List of Dragon Ball Super episodes</a></div>
<p>On April 28, 2015, Toei Animation announced <i>Dragon Ball Super</i><span style="font-weight: normal"> (<span lang="ja" title="Japanese language text">ドラゴンボール超</span>, <i lang="ja-Latn" title="Hepburn transliteration">Doragon Bōru Sūpā</i>)</span>, the first all-new <i>Dragon Ball</i> television series to be released in 18 years. It debuted on July 5 and ran as a weekly series at 9:00 am on Fuji TV on Sundays until its series finale on March 25, 2018 after 131 episodes.<sup id="cite_ref-DBSdebut_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DBSdebut-125">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Masako_Nozawa" title="Masako Nozawa">Masako Nozawa</a> reprises her roles as Goku, Gohan, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Dragon_Ball_characters#Goten" title="List of Dragon Ball characters">Goten</a>. Most of the original cast reprise their roles as well.<sup id="cite_ref-creditsDBS_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-creditsDBS-126">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-castDBS_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-castDBS-127">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Koichi_Yamadera" class="mw-redirect" title="Koichi Yamadera">Koichi Yamadera</a> and <a href="/wiki/Masakazu_Morita" title="Masakazu Morita">Masakazu Morita</a> also reprise their roles, as <a href="/wiki/Beerus" title="Beerus">Beerus</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Dragon_Ball_characters#Whis" title="List of Dragon Ball characters">Whis</a>, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-castDBS_127-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-castDBS-127">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The story of the anime is set four years after the defeat of <a href="/wiki/Majin_Buu" title="Majin Buu">Majin Buu</a>, when the Earth has become peaceful once again. Akira Toriyama is credited as the original creator, as well for "original story &amp; character design concepts."<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> It is also being adapted into a parallel manga.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Manga-inspired_series">Manga-inspired series</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dragon_Ball&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Manga-inspired series">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>Dragon Ball GT</i> and <i>Super Dragon Ball Heroes</i> are not originated from any direct source material from Toriyama, being fully created by their respective animation studios.
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Dragon_Ball_GT"><i>Dragon Ball GT</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dragon_Ball&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Dragon Ball GT">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Dragon_Ball_GT" title="Dragon Ball GT">Dragon Ball GT</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Dragon_Ball_GT_episodes" title="List of Dragon Ball GT episodes">List of Dragon Ball GT episodes</a></div>
<p><i>Dragon Ball GT</i><span style="font-weight: normal"> (<span lang="ja" title="Japanese language text">ドラゴンボールGT(ジーティー)</span>, <i lang="ja-Latn" title="Hepburn transliteration">Doragon Bōru Jī Tī</i>, <i>G(rand) T(ouring)</i><sup id="cite_ref-GTDragonBox_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GTDragonBox-130">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>)</span> premiered on Fuji TV on February 7, 1996 and ran until November 19, 1997 for 64 episodes.<sup id="cite_ref-AnimeEncyc_7-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AnimeEncyc-7">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Unlike the first two anime series, it is not based on Akira Toriyama's original <i>Dragon Ball</i> manga,<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> being created by Toei Animation as a sequel to the series or as Toriyama called it, a "<a href="/wiki/Gaiden" class="mw-redirect" title="Gaiden">grand side story</a> of the original <i>Dragon Ball.</i>"<sup id="cite_ref-GTDragonBox_130-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GTDragonBox-130">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> Toriyama designed the main cast, the spaceship used in the show, the design of three planets, and came up with the title and logo. In addition to this, Toriyama also oversaw production of the series, just as he had for the <i>Dragon Ball</i> and <i>Dragon Ball Z</i> anime. The television special episode, <i>Goku's Side Story! The Proof of his Courage is the Four-Star Ball</i>, or <i><a href="/wiki/Dragon_Ball_GT:_A_Hero%27s_Legacy" title="Dragon Ball GT: A Hero&#39;s Legacy">A Hero's Legacy</a></i> as Funimation titled it for their dub, aired on March 26, 1997, between episodes 41 and 42, serving as a kind of precursor to the epilogue to the series shown at the end of episode 64.
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Super_Dragon_Ball_Heroes"><i>Super Dragon Ball Heroes</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dragon_Ball&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Super Dragon Ball Heroes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Super_Dragon_Ball_Heroes_(anime)" title="Super Dragon Ball Heroes (anime)">Super Dragon Ball Heroes (anime)</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Super_Dragon_Ball_Heroes_episodes" title="List of Super Dragon Ball Heroes episodes">List of Super Dragon Ball Heroes episodes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dragon_Ball_Heroes" title="Dragon Ball Heroes">Dragon Ball Heroes</a></div><p>
In 2018, an anime to promote the <i><a href="/wiki/Dragon_Ball_Heroes" title="Dragon Ball Heroes">Super Dragon Ball Heroes</a></i> card and video game series was announced with a July 1 premiere.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> The series' announcement included a brief synopsis:</p><blockquote><p>Trunks returns from the future to train with Goku and Vegeta. However, he abruptly vanishes. The mysterious man "Fu" suddenly appears, telling them that Trunks has been locked up on the "Prison Planet", a mysterious facility in an unknown location between universes. The group searches for the Dragon Balls to free Trunks, but an unending super battle awaits them! Will Goku and the others manage to rescue Trunks and escape the Prison Planet?</p></blockquote>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_installments">Other installments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dragon_Ball&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Other installments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The short film <i><a href="/wiki/Dragon_Ball:_Yo!_Son_Goku_and_His_Friends_Return!!" title="Dragon Ball: Yo! Son Goku and His Friends Return!!">Dragon Ball: Yo! Son Goku and His Friends Return!!</a></i> was created for the Jump Super Anime Tour,<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> which celebrated <i>Weekly Shōnen Jump</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> 40th anniversary, and debuted on September 21, 2008. A short animated adaptation of Naho Ōishi's Bardock spinoff manga, <i><a href="/wiki/Dragon_Ball:_Episode_of_Bardock" title="Dragon Ball: Episode of Bardock">Dragon Ball: Episode of Bardock</a></i>, was shown on December 17–18, 2011 at the Jump Festa 2012 event.<sup id="cite_ref-info_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-info-134">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A two-episode <a href="/wiki/Original_video_animation" title="Original video animation">original video animation (OVA)</a>  titled <i><a href="/wiki/Dragon_Ball_Z_Side_Story:_Plan_to_Eradicate_the_Saiyans" title="Dragon Ball Z Side Story: Plan to Eradicate the Saiyans">Dragon Ball Z Side Story: Plan to Eradicate the Saiyans</a></i> was created in 1993 as <a href="/wiki/Strategy_guide" title="Strategy guide">strategy guides</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Nintendo_Entertainment_System" title="Nintendo Entertainment System">Famicom</a> video game of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Dragon_Ball_video_games#1990s" title="List of Dragon Ball video games">same name</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> A remake titled <i><a href="/wiki/Dragon_Ball:_Plan_to_Eradicate_the_Super_Saiyans" title="Dragon Ball: Plan to Eradicate the Super Saiyans">Dragon Ball: Plan to Eradicate the Super Saiyans</a></i> was created as a bonus feature for the <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_3" title="PlayStation 3">PlayStation 3</a> and <a href="/wiki/Xbox_360" title="Xbox 360">Xbox 360</a> video game <i><a href="/wiki/Dragon_Ball:_Raging_Blast_2" title="Dragon Ball: Raging Blast 2">Dragon Ball: Raging Blast 2</a></i>, which was released on November 11, 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A two-part hour-long crossover special between <i>Dragon Ball Z</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/One_Piece" title="One Piece">One Piece</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Toriko" title="Toriko">Toriko</a></i>, referred to as <i><a href="/wiki/Dream_9_Toriko_%26_One_Piece_%26_Dragon_Ball_Z_Super_Collaboration_Special!!" title="Dream 9 Toriko &amp; One Piece &amp; Dragon Ball Z Super Collaboration Special!!">Dream 9 Toriko &amp; One Piece &amp; Dragon Ball Z Super Collaboration Special!!</a></i> aired on April 7, 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-crossover_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crossover-137">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reception_2">Reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dragon_Ball&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The anime adaptations have also been very well-received and are better known in the Western world than the manga, with Anime News Network saying, "Few anime series have mainstreamed it the way <i>Dragon Ball Z</i> has. To a certain generation of television consumers its characters are as well known as any in the animated realm, and for many it was the first step into the wilderness of anime fandom."<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> In 2000, satellite TV channel <a href="/wiki/Animax" title="Animax">Animax</a> together with <i><a href="/wiki/Brutus_(magazine)" title="Brutus (magazine)">Brutus</a></i>, a men's lifestyle magazine, and <a href="/wiki/Culture_Convenience_Club" title="Culture Convenience Club">Tsutaya</a>, Japan's largest video rental chain, conducted a poll among 200,000 fans on the top anime series, with <i>Dragon Ball</i> coming in fourth.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/TV_Asahi" title="TV Asahi">TV Asahi</a> conducted two polls in 2005 on the Top 100 Anime, <i>Dragon Ball</i> came in second in the nationwide survey conducted with multiple age-groups and in third in the online poll.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i>Dragon Ball</i> is one of the most successful franchises in animation history.<sup id="cite_ref-latimes_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-latimes-142">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> The anime series is broadcast in more than 80<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>countries worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-gamebiz_118-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gamebiz-118">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> In Japan, the first <a href="/wiki/List_of_Dragon_Ball_films" title="List of Dragon Ball films">sixteen anime films</a> up until <i><a href="/wiki/Dragon_Ball_Z:_Wrath_of_the_Dragon" title="Dragon Ball Z: Wrath of the Dragon">Dragon Ball Z: Wrath of the Dragon</a></i> (1995) sold 50<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million tickets and grossed over <span style="white-space: nowrap">¥40 billion</span> (<span style="white-space: nowrap">$501 million</span>) at the box office, in addition to selling over 500,000 <a href="/wiki/Home_video" title="Home video">home video</a> units, by 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> Later <a href="/wiki/DVD" title="DVD">DVD</a> releases of the <i>Dragon Ball</i> anime series have topped Japan's sales charts on several occasions.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> In the United States, the anime series sold over 25<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million DVD units by January 2012,<sup id="cite_ref-Funimation_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Funimation-147">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> and has sold more than 30<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million DVD and <a href="/wiki/Blu-ray" title="Blu-ray">Blu-ray</a> units as of 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-latimes_142-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-latimes-142">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a>, public screenings of the <i>Dragon Ball Super</i> finale in 2018 filled public spaces and stadiums in cities across the region, including stadiums holding tens of thousands of spectators.<sup id="cite_ref-wired_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wired-148">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Carl Kimlinger of Anime News Network summed up <i>Dragon Ball</i> as "an action-packed tale told with rare humor and something even rarer—a genuine sense of adventure."<sup id="cite_ref-DBseason2_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DBseason2-149">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> Both Kimlinger and colleague Theron Martin noted Funimation's reputation for drastic alterations of the script, but praised the dub.<sup id="cite_ref-DBseason2_149-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DBseason2-149">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DBseason3_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DBseason3-150">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> However, some critics and most fans of the Japanese version have been more critical with Funimation's English dub and script of <i>Dragon Ball Z</i> over the years. Jeffrey Harris of <a href="/wiki/IGN" title="IGN">IGN</a> criticized the voices, including how Freeza's appearance combined with the feminine English voice left fans confused about Freeza's gender.<sup id="cite_ref-IGN_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IGN-151">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> Carlos Ross of T.H.E.M. Anime Reviews considered the series' characters to be different from stereotypical stock characters and noted that they undergo much more development.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> Despite praising <i>Dragon Ball Z</i> for its cast of characters, they criticized it for having long and repetitive fights.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i>Dragon Ball Z</i> is well-known, and often criticized, for its long, repetitive, dragged-out fights that span several episodes, with Martin commenting "DBZ practically turned drawing out fights into an art form."<sup id="cite_ref-DBZSeason6_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DBZSeason6-154">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> However, Jason Thompson of io9 explained that this comes from the fact that the anime was being created alongside the manga.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> <i>Dragon Ball Z</i> was listed as the 78th best animated show in <a href="/wiki/IGN" title="IGN">IGN</a>'s Top 100 Animated Series,<sup id="cite_ref-ign100_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ign100-156">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> and was also listed as the 50th greatest cartoon in <a href="/wiki/Wizard_(magazine)" title="Wizard (magazine)"><i>Wizard</i> magazine</a>'s Top 100 Greatest Cartoons list.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Harris commented that <i>Dragon Ball GT</i> "is downright repellent", mentioning that the material and characters had lost their novelty and fun. He also criticized the <i>GT</i> character designs of <a href="/wiki/Trunks_(Dragon_Ball)" title="Trunks (Dragon Ball)">Trunks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vegeta" title="Vegeta">Vegeta</a> as being goofy.<sup id="cite_ref-IGN_151-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IGN-151">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> Zac Bertschy of Anime News Network also gave negative comments about <i>GT</i>, mentioning that the fights from the series were "a very simple childish exercise" and that many other anime were superior. The plot of <i>Dragon Ball GT</i> has also been criticized for giving a formula that was already used in its predecessors.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The first episode of <i>Dragon Ball Z Kai</i> earned a viewer ratings percentage of 11.3, ahead of <i><a href="/wiki/One_Piece" title="One Piece">One Piece</a></i> and behind <i><a href="/wiki/Crayon_Shin-chan" title="Crayon Shin-chan">Crayon Shin-chan</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> Although following episodes had lower ratings, <i>Kai</i> was among the top 10 anime in viewer ratings every week in Japan for most of its run.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_media">Other media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dragon_Ball&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Other media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Dragon_Ball_films" title="List of Dragon Ball films">List of Dragon Ball films</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Anime_films">Anime films</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dragon_Ball&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Anime films">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Twenty animated theatrical films based on the <i>Dragon Ball</i> series have been released in Japan. The three most recent films, <i><a href="/wiki/Dragon_Ball_Z:_Battle_of_Gods" title="Dragon Ball Z: Battle of Gods">Dragon Ball Z: Battle of Gods</a></i> (2013), <i><a href="/wiki/Dragon_Ball_Z:_Resurrection_%27F%27" title="Dragon Ball Z: Resurrection &#39;F&#39;">Dragon Ball Z: Resurrection 'F'</a></i> (2015) and <i><a href="/wiki/Dragon_Ball_Super:_Broly" title="Dragon Ball Super: Broly">Dragon Ball Super: Broly</a></i> (2018), were produced as full-length feature films and were given stand-alone theatrical releases in Japan (as well as limited theatrical releases in the U.S.). They're also the first movies to have original creator Akira Toriyama deeply involved in their production; <i>Battle of Gods</i> and <i>Resurrection 'F'</i> were remade into the first and second arcs of the <i>Dragon Ball Super</i> anime, which told the same stories as the two films in expanded detail.<sup id="cite_ref-BattleGods_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BattleGods-162">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> The 1996 feature film, <i><a href="/wiki/Dragon_Ball:_The_Path_to_Power" title="Dragon Ball: The Path to Power">Dragon Ball: The Path to Power</a></i>, was also a full-length theatrical release with a running time of 80 minutes, and was produced to coincide with the 10th anniversary of the anime as a re-imagining of the first few arcs of the series.
</p><p>All previous films were mostly below <a href="/wiki/Feature_length" title="Feature length">feature length</a> (around 45–60 minutes each), making them only slightly longer than one or two episodes of the TV series; this is due to them being originally shown as back-to-back presentations alongside other Toei film productions. These films are also mostly alternate re-tellings of certain story arcs (like <i>The Path to Power</i>), or extra side-stories that do not correlate with the continuity of the series. The first three films, along with <i>The Path to Power</i>, are based on the original <i>Dragon Ball</i> anime series. The remaining thirteen older films are based on <i>Dragon Ball Z</i>. The first five films were shown at the Toei Manga Festival<span style="font-weight: normal"> (<span lang="ja" title="Japanese language text"><a href="https://ja.wikipedia.org/wiki/%E6%9D%B1%E6%98%A0%E3%81%BE%E3%82%93%E3%81%8C%E3%81%BE%E3%81%A4%E3%82%8A" class="extiw" title="ja:東映まんがまつり">東映まんがまつり</a></span>, <i lang="ja-Latn" title="Hepburn transliteration">Tōei Manga Matsuri</i>)</span>, while the sixth through seventeenth films were shown at the Toei Anime Fair<span style="font-weight: normal"> (<span lang="ja" title="Japanese language text"><a href="https://ja.wikipedia.org/wiki/%E6%9D%B1%E6%98%A0%E3%82%A2%E3%83%8B%E3%83%A1%E3%83%95%E3%82%A7%E3%82%A2" class="extiw" title="ja:東映アニメフェア">東映アニメフェア</a></span>, <i lang="ja-Latn" title="Hepburn transliteration">Toei Anime Fea</i>)</span>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Live-action_film">Live-action film</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dragon_Ball&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Live-action film">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>An American live-action film titled <i><a href="/wiki/Dragonball_Evolution" title="Dragonball Evolution">Dragonball Evolution</a></i> was produced by <a href="/wiki/20th_Century_Fox" class="mw-redirect" title="20th Century Fox">20th Century Fox</a> after it acquired the <a href="/wiki/Feature_film" title="Feature film">feature film</a> rights to the <i>Dragon Ball</i> franchise in March 2002. Previous to the film, two unofficial live-action films had been produced decades prior.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-itsofficial_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-itsofficial-165">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> The film was directed by <a href="/wiki/James_Wong_(producer)" class="mw-redirect" title="James Wong (producer)">James Wong</a> and produced by <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Chow" title="Stephen Chow">Stephen Chow</a>, it was released in the United States on April 10, 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-itsofficial_165-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-itsofficial-165">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FoxJapan_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FoxJapan-166">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> The film was meant to lead into sequels,<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>
which were cancelled, after the film flopped at the box office and became universally heralded as one of the worst adaptations of all time, being considered by the fans as being unfaithful to the source material.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> Franchise creator Akira Toriyama also criticized the film adding he was completely left out of the creative process, despite having himself offered to help, going as far as saying: "the result was a movie, I couldn't even call <i>Dragon Ball</i>".<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> Years after its release, the writer of the film, Ben Ramsey, released a public apology in which he admitted to have written the film "chasing for a payday" instead of "as a fan of the franchise".<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>With the news of <a href="/wiki/Acquisition_of_21st_Century_Fox_by_Disney" title="Acquisition of 21st Century Fox by Disney">20th Century Fox selling itself</a>, its assets; which include the film rights to the <i>Dragon Ball</i> franchise, will now be owned by its purchaser, <a href="/wiki/The_Walt_Disney_Company" title="The Walt Disney Company">The Walt Disney Company</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Theme_park_attractions">Theme park attractions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dragon_Ball&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Theme park attractions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>"Dragon Ball Z: The Real 4D" debuted at <a href="/wiki/Universal_Studios_Japan" title="Universal Studios Japan">Universal Studios Japan</a> in the summer of 2016. It features a battle between Goku and Freeza. Unlike most <i>Dragon Ball</i> animation, the attraction is animated with <a href="/wiki/Computer_animation" title="Computer animation">CGI</a>. A second attraction titled "Dragon Ball Z: The Real 4-D at Super Tenkaichi Budokai" debuted at Universal Studios Japan in the summer of 2017, which featured a battle between the heroes and <a href="/wiki/Broly" title="Broly">Broly</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Video_games">Video games</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dragon_Ball&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Video games">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Dragon_Ball_video_games" title="List of Dragon Ball video games">List of Dragon Ball video games</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dragon_Ball_Z_arcade_conversion_kit_by_Banpresto.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/ea/Dragon_Ball_Z_arcade_conversion_kit_by_Banpresto.jpg/220px-Dragon_Ball_Z_arcade_conversion_kit_by_Banpresto.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/ea/Dragon_Ball_Z_arcade_conversion_kit_by_Banpresto.jpg/330px-Dragon_Ball_Z_arcade_conversion_kit_by_Banpresto.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/e/ea/Dragon_Ball_Z_arcade_conversion_kit_by_Banpresto.jpg 2x" data-file-width="387" data-file-height="257" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dragon_Ball_Z_arcade_conversion_kit_by_Banpresto.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <i>Dragon Ball Z</i> arcade conversion kit that includes the PCB, instructions and operator's manual</div></div></div>
<p>The <i>Dragon Ball</i> franchise has spawned multiple video games across various genres and platforms. Earlier games of the series included a system of card battling and were released for the <a href="/wiki/Nintendo_Entertainment_System" title="Nintendo Entertainment System">Famicom</a> following the storyline of the series.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> Starting with the <a href="/wiki/Super_Nintendo_Entertainment_System" title="Super Nintendo Entertainment System">Super Famicom</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sega_Genesis" title="Sega Genesis">Mega Drive</a>, most of the games were from the <a href="/wiki/Fighting_game" title="Fighting game">fighting</a> genre or RPG (Role Playing Game), such as the <i>Super Butoden</i> series.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> The first <i>Dragon Ball</i> game to be released in the United States was <i><a href="/wiki/Dragon_Ball_GT:_Final_Bout" title="Dragon Ball GT: Final Bout">Dragon Ball GT: Final Bout</a></i> for the <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_(console)" title="PlayStation (console)">PlayStation</a> in 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> For the <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_2" title="PlayStation 2">PlayStation 2</a> and <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_Portable" title="PlayStation Portable">PlayStation Portable</a> games the characters were redone in 3D <a href="/wiki/Cel-shaded" class="mw-redirect" title="Cel-shaded">cel-shaded</a> graphics. These games included the <i><a href="/wiki/Dragon_Ball_Z:_Budokai" title="Dragon Ball Z: Budokai">Dragon Ball Z: Budokai</a></i> series and the <i><a href="/wiki/Dragon_Ball_Z:_Budokai_Tenkaichi" title="Dragon Ball Z: Budokai Tenkaichi">Dragon Ball Z: Budokai Tenkaichi</a></i> series.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Dragon_Ball_Z:_Burst_Limit" title="Dragon Ball Z: Burst Limit">Dragon Ball Z: Burst Limit</a></i> was the first game of the franchise developed for the <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_3" title="PlayStation 3">PlayStation 3</a> and <a href="/wiki/Xbox_360" title="Xbox 360">Xbox 360</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Dragon_Ball_Xenoverse" title="Dragon Ball Xenoverse">Dragon Ball Xenoverse</a></i> was the first game of the franchise developed for the <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_4" title="PlayStation 4">PlayStation 4</a> and <a href="/wiki/Xbox_One" title="Xbox One">Xbox One</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Massively_multiplayer_online_role-playing_game" title="Massively multiplayer online role-playing game">massively multiplayer online role-playing game</a> called <i><a href="/wiki/Dragon_Ball_Online" title="Dragon Ball Online">Dragon Ball Online</a></i> was available in Korea, Hong Kong and Taiwan until the servers were shut down in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> A few years later fans started recreating the game. Today, "Dragon Ball Online Global" is a new, European version of <i>Dragon Ball Online</i> and it is being developed, while open beta server is running.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> A quite notable recent release is <a href="/wiki/Dragon_Ball_FighterZ" title="Dragon Ball FighterZ">Dragon Ball FighterZ</a> a game of the <a href="/wiki/Fighting_game" title="Fighting game">Fighting game</a> genre. Developed by <a href="/wiki/Arc_System_Works" title="Arc System Works">Arc System Works</a> of which the game had received massive fan and critical acclaim for its fast paced frantic 3V3 battles, and great visuals, also winning Best Fighting Game of 2018 at the <a href="/wiki/The_Game_Awards" title="The Game Awards">Game Awards</a><sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> and many other awards and other nominations. It has also seen a large <a href="/wiki/Esports" title="Esports">Esports</a> scene. It also did commercially very well, selling 4 million units<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> across all platforms.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Merchandise">Merchandise</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dragon_Ball&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Merchandise">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Soundtracks">Soundtracks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dragon_Ball&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Soundtracks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Dragon_Ball_soundtracks" title="List of Dragon Ball soundtracks">List of Dragon Ball soundtracks</a></div>
<p>Myriad soundtracks were released in the anime, movies and the games. The music for the first two anime <i>Dragon Ball</i> and <i>Z</i> and its films was composed by <a href="/wiki/Shunsuke_Kikuchi" title="Shunsuke Kikuchi">Shunsuke Kikuchi</a>, while the music from <i>GT</i> was composed by Akihito Tokunaga and the music from <i>Kai</i> was composed by Kenji Yamamoto and Norihito Sumitomo. For the first anime, the soundtracks released were <i><a href="/wiki/Dragon_Ball:_Music_Collection" title="Dragon Ball: Music Collection">Dragon Ball: Music Collection</a></i> in 1985 and <i><a href="/wiki/Dragon_Ball:_Complete_Song_Collection" title="Dragon Ball: Complete Song Collection">Dragon Ball: Complete Song Collection</a></i> in 1991, although they were reissued in 2007 and 2003, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> For the second anime, the soundtrack series released were <i><a href="/wiki/Dragon_Ball_Z_Hit_Song_Collection_Series" class="mw-redirect" title="Dragon Ball Z Hit Song Collection Series">Dragon Ball Z Hit Song Collection Series</a></i>. It was produced and released by <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Records" title="Columbia Records">Columbia Records</a> of Japan from July 21, 1989 to March 20, 1996 the show's entire lifespan. On September 20, 2006 Columbia re-released the Hit Song Collection on their Animex 1300 series.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> Other CDs released are compilations, video games and films soundtracks as well as music from the English versions.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Companion_books">Companion books</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dragon_Ball&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Companion books">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Db_TCI.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d0/Db_TCI.jpg/170px-Db_TCI.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="250" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d0/Db_TCI.jpg/255px-Db_TCI.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/d/d0/Db_TCI.jpg 2x" data-file-width="260" data-file-height="382" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Db_TCI.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cover of <i>Dragon Ball: The Complete Illustrations</i></div></div></div>
<p>There have been numerous companion books to the <i>Dragon Ball</i> franchise. Chief among these are the <i>Daizenshuu</i><span style="font-weight: normal"> (<span lang="ja" title="Japanese language text">大全集</span>)</span> series, comprising seven hardback main volumes and three supplemental softcover volumes, covering the manga and the first two anime series and their theatrical films. The first of these, <i>Dragon Ball: The Complete Illustrations</i> (<i>Daizenshuu</i> volume 1), first published in Japan in 1995, is the only one that was released in English, being printed in 2008 by Viz Media.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> It contains all 264 colored illustrations Akira Toriyama drew for the <i>Weekly Shōnen Jump</i> magazines' covers, bonus giveaways and specials, and all the covers for the 42 <i>tankōbon</i>. It also includes an interview with Toriyama on his work process. The remainder have never been released in English, and all are now out of print in Japan. From February 4 to May 9, 2013, condensed versions of the <i>Daizenshuu</i> with some updated information were released as the four-volume <i>Chōzenshū</i><span style="font-weight: normal"> (<span lang="ja" title="Japanese language text">超全集</span>)</span> series.<sup id="cite_ref-colorchozenshuu_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-colorchozenshuu-32">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> For <i>Dragon Ball GT</i>, the <i>Dragon Ball GT Perfect Files</i> were released in May and December 1997 by <a href="/wiki/Shueisha" title="Shueisha">Shueisha</a>'s <i>Jump Comics Selection</i> imprint. They include series information, illustration galleries, behind-the-scenes information, and more. They were out of print for many years, but were re-released in April 2006 (accompanying the Japanese DVD release of <i>Dragon Ball GT</i>) and this edition is still in print.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Coinciding with the 34-volume <i>kanzenban</i> re-release of the manga, and the release of the entire series on DVD for the first time in Japan, four new guidebooks were released in 2003 and 2004. <i>Dragon Ball Landmark</i> and <i>Dragon Ball Forever</i> cover the manga, using volume numbers for story points that reference the <i>kanzenban</i> release,<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> while <i>Dragon Ball: Tenkaichi Densetsu</i><span style="font-weight: normal"> (<span lang="ja" title="Japanese language text">ドラゴンボール 天下一伝説</span>)</span> and <i>Dragon Ball Z: Son Goku Densetsu</i><span style="font-weight: normal"> (<span lang="ja" title="Japanese language text">ドラゴンボールZ 孫悟空伝説</span>)</span> cover the <i>Dragon Ball</i> and <i>Dragon Ball Z</i> anime, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> Much of the material in these books is reused from the earlier <i>Daizenshuu</i> volumes, but they include new textual material including substantial interviews with the creator, cast and production staff of the series. <i>Son Goku Densetsu</i> in particular showcases previously-unpublished design sketches of Goku's father Bardock, drawn by character designer Katsuyoshi Nakatsuru prior to creator Akira Toriyama's revisions that resulted in the final version.
</p><p>Following the release of <i>Dragon Ball Kai</i> in Japan, four new guidebooks were released: the two-volume <i>Dragon Ball: Super Exciting Guide</i><span style="font-weight: normal"> (<span lang="ja" title="Japanese language text">ドラゴンボール 超エキサイティングガイド</span>)</span> in 2009, covering the manga,<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> and two-volume <i>Dragon Ball: Extreme Battle Collection</i><span style="font-weight: normal"> (<span lang="ja" title="Japanese language text">ドラゴンボール　極限バトルコレクション</span>)</span> in 2010, covering the anime series.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> Despite the TV series airing during this time being <i>Kai</i>, the <i>Extreme Battle Collection</i> books reference the earlier <i>Z</i> series in content and episode numbers. These books also include new question-and-answer sessions with Akira Toriyama, revealing a few new details about the world and characters of the series. 2010 also saw the release of a new artbook, <i>Dragon Ball: Anime Illustrations Guide – The Golden Warrior</i><span style="font-weight: normal"> (<span lang="ja" title="Japanese language text">ドラゴンボール アニメイラスト集 「黄金の戦士」</span>)</span>; a sort of anime-counterpart to the manga-oriented <i>Complete Illustrations</i>, it showcases anime-original illustrations and includes interviews with the three principal character designers for the anime. Each of the Japanese "Dragon Box" DVD releases of the series and movies, which were released from 2003 to 2006, as well as the Blu-ray boxed sets of <i>Dragon Ball Kai</i>, released 2009 to 2011, come with a <i>Dragon Book</i> guide that contains details about the content therein. Each also contains a new interview with a member of the cast or staff of the series. These books have been reproduced textually for Funimation's release of the <i>Dragon Ball Z</i> Dragon Box sets from 2009 to 2011.
</p><p><b>Collectible cards</b>
</p>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Dragon_Ball_Collectible_Card_Game" title="Dragon Ball Collectible Card Game">Dragon Ball Collectible Card Game</a></div>
<p>Collectible cards based on the <i>Dragon Ball</i>, <i>Dragon Ball Z</i>, and <i>Dragon Ball GT</i> series have been released by <a href="/wiki/Bandai" title="Bandai">Bandai</a>. These cards feature various scenes from the manga and anime stills, plus exclusive artwork from all three series. Bandai released the first set in the United States in July 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>Tabletop role-playing game</b>
</p>
<ul><li><i><a href="/wiki/Dragon_Ball_Z:_The_Anime_Adventure_Game" title="Dragon Ball Z: The Anime Adventure Game">Dragon Ball Z: The Anime Adventure Game</a></i>, a <a href="/wiki/Tabletop_role-playing_game" title="Tabletop role-playing game">tabletop role-playing game</a> produced by <a href="/wiki/R._Talsorian_Games" title="R. Talsorian Games">R. Talsorian Games</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-review_202-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-review-202">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
