<p><i>Dragon Ball</i> is one of the top twenty <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_highest-grossing_media_franchises" class="mw-redirect" title="List of the highest-grossing media franchises">highest-grossing media franchises of all time</a>, having generated an estimated <span style="white-space: nowrap">$30 billion</span> in total franchise revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-Legend144_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Legend144-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> By 2011, the franchise had generated <span style="white-space: nowrap">$5 billion</span> in merchandise sales.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> In 2012, the franchise grossed <span style="white-space: nowrap">¥7.67 billion</span> (<span style="white-space: nowrap">$96.13 million</span>) from licensed merchandise sales in Japan.<sup id="cite_ref-charabiz_216-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-charabiz-216">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup> Bandai also sold over 2<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>billion <i>Dragon Ball</i> <a href="/wiki/Carddass" title="Carddass">Carddass</a> cards in Japan by 1998,<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> and over 1<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million Dragon Stars figurines in the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a> and Europe as of 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> As of 2019, the <a href="/wiki/Mobile_game" title="Mobile game">mobile game</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Dragon_Ball_Z:_Dokkan_Battle" title="Dragon Ball Z: Dokkan Battle">Dragon Ball Z: Dokkan Battle</a></i> has received over 300<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million downloads worldwide,<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/Dragon_Ball_FighterZ" title="Dragon Ball FighterZ">Dragon Ball FighterZ</a></i> is one of the most popular <a href="/wiki/ESports" class="mw-redirect" title="ESports">eSports</a> <a href="/wiki/Fighting_games" class="mw-redirect" title="Fighting games">fighting games</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-wired_148-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wired-148">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Popular_culture">Popular culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dragon_Ball&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Popular culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Since its debut, <i>Dragon Ball</i> has had a considerable impact on global <a href="/wiki/Popular_culture" title="Popular culture">popular culture</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-wired_148-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wired-148">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cleveland_220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cleveland-220">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup> In 2015, the Japan Anniversary Association officially declared May 9 as "Goku Day"<span style="font-weight: normal"> (<span lang="ja" title="Japanese language text">悟空の日</span>, <i lang="ja-Latn" title="Hepburn transliteration">Gokū no Hi</i>)</span>; in Japanese, the numbers five and nine can be pronounced as "Go" and "Ku".<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup> It is similarly influential in international popular culture across other parts of the world.<sup id="cite_ref-wired_148-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wired-148">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> <i>Dragon Ball</i> is widely referenced in <a href="/wiki/American_popular_culture" class="mw-redirect" title="American popular culture">American popular culture</a>, from television and music to celebrities and athletes, and the show has been celebrated with Goku making an appearance at the 2018 <a href="/wiki/Macy%27s_Thanksgiving_Day_Parade" title="Macy&#39;s Thanksgiving Day Parade">Macy's Thanksgiving Day Parade</a>, and with <i>Dragon Ball</i> <a href="/wiki/Mural" title="Mural">murals</a> appearing in cities such as <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kansas_City" class="mw-redirect" title="Kansas City">Kansas City</a> and <a href="/wiki/Denver" title="Denver">Denver</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cleveland_220-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cleveland-220">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i>Dragon Ball</i> is also immensely popular in other regions of the world, such as <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a>, where public screenings of the <i>Dragon Ball Super</i> finale in 2018 filled public spaces and stadiums in cities across the region, including stadiums holding tens of thousands of spectators.<sup id="cite_ref-wired_148-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wired-148">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> <i>Dragon Ball</i> creator Akira Toriyama was decorated a <i>Chevalier</i> or "Knight" of the <a href="/wiki/Ordre_des_Arts_et_des_Lettres" title="Ordre des Arts et des Lettres">Ordre des Arts et des Lettres</a> by the French government in May 2019 for his contributions to the arts, particularly for <i>Dragon Ball</i> which has been credited with popularizing manga in France.<sup id="cite_ref-recluse_222-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-recluse-222">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Vegeta" title="Vegeta">Vegeta</a>'s quote "<a href="/wiki/It%27s_Over_9000!" title="It&#39;s Over 9000!">It's Over 9000!</a>" from the <a href="/wiki/Saiyan_Saga" class="mw-redirect" title="Saiyan Saga">Saiyan Saga</a> in the English dub of <i>Dragon Ball Z</i> is a popular <a href="/wiki/Internet_meme" title="Internet meme">internet meme</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup> Mark Sammut of <i>TheGamer</i> notes that <a href="/wiki/Gohan" title="Gohan">Gohan</a> occasionally performs the <a href="/wiki/Dab_(dance)" title="Dab (dance)">dab</a> move (as <a href="/wiki/The_Great_Saiyaman" class="mw-redirect" title="The Great Saiyaman">The Great Saiyaman</a>), decades before it became a popular dance move in <a href="/wiki/American_popular_culture" class="mw-redirect" title="American popular culture">American popular culture</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Goku has been identified as a <a href="/wiki/Superhero" title="Superhero">superhero</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup> as well as Gohan with his Great Saiyaman persona.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Motorola" title="Motorola">Motorola</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Freescale_DragonBall" title="Freescale DragonBall">Freescale DragonBall</a> and DragonBall EZ/VZ <a href="/wiki/Microcontroller" title="Microcontroller">microcontroller</a> processors, released in 1995, are named after <i>Dragon Ball</i> and <i>Dragon Ball Z</i>, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Comics_and_animation">Comics and animation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dragon_Ball&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Comics and animation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>Dragon Ball</i> has been cited as inspiration across various different media. <i>Dragon Ball</i> is credited with setting trends for popular <a href="/wiki/Sh%C5%8Dnen_manga" title="Shōnen manga">shōnen manga</a> and anime since the 1980s, with manga critic <a href="/wiki/Jason_Thompson_(writer)" title="Jason Thompson (writer)">Jason Thompson</a> in 2011 calling it "by far the most influential shōnen manga of the last 30 years." Successful shōnen manga authors such as <a href="/wiki/Eiichiro_Oda" title="Eiichiro Oda">Eiichiro Oda</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/One_Piece" title="One Piece">One Piece</a></i>), <a href="/wiki/Masashi_Kishimoto" title="Masashi Kishimoto">Masashi Kishimoto</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Naruto" title="Naruto">Naruto</a></i>), <a href="/wiki/Tite_Kubo" title="Tite Kubo">Tite Kubo</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Bleach_(manga)" title="Bleach (manga)">Bleach</a></i>), <a href="/wiki/Hiro_Mashima" title="Hiro Mashima">Hiro Mashima</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Fairy_Tail" title="Fairy Tail">Fairy Tail</a></i>) and <a href="/wiki/Kentaro_Yabuki" title="Kentaro Yabuki">Kentaro Yabuki</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Black_Cat_(manga)" title="Black Cat (manga)">Black Cat</a></i>) have cited <i>Dragon Ball</i> as an influence on their own now popular works. According to Thompson, "almost every <i>Shonen Jump</i> artist lists it as one of their favorites and lifts from it in various ways."<sup id="cite_ref-ANNJT_108-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ANNJT-108">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Ian_Jones-Quartey" title="Ian Jones-Quartey">Ian Jones-Quartey</a>, a producer of the American animated series <i><a href="/wiki/Steven_Universe" title="Steven Universe">Steven Universe</a></i>, is a fan of <i>Dragon Ball</i> and <i>Dr. Slump</i>, and uses Toriyama's vehicle designs as a reference for his own. He also stated that "We're all big Toriyama fans on [<i>Steven Universe</i>], which kind of shows a bit."<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Comic_book" title="Comic book">Comic book</a> artist André Lima Araújo cited <i>Dragon Ball</i>, along with several other manga and anime, as a major influence on his work, which includes <a href="/wiki/Marvel_comics" class="mw-redirect" title="Marvel comics">Marvel comics</a> such as <i><a href="/wiki/Age_of_Ultron" title="Age of Ultron">Age of Ultron</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Avengers_A.I." title="Avengers A.I.">Avengers A.I.</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Spider-Verse" title="Spider-Verse">Spider-Verse</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Inhumans" class="mw-redirect" title="The Inhumans">The Inhumans</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup> Filipino comic artist Dexter Soy, who has worked on Marvel and <a href="/wiki/DC_comics" class="mw-redirect" title="DC comics">DC comics</a> such as <i><a href="/wiki/Captain_America" title="Captain America">Captain America</a></i>, cited <i>Dragon Ball</i> as a major inspiration.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Iron_Man" title="Iron Man">Tony Stark: Iron Man</a></i> #11 (2019)  makes references to <i>Dragon Ball Z</i>, including <a href="/wiki/Miles_Morales" title="Miles Morales">Miles Morales</a> as <a href="/wiki/Spider-Man" title="Spider-Man">Spider-Man</a> referencing the Super Saiyan transformation.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Film">Film</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dragon_Ball&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Film">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>An unofficial live-action <a href="/wiki/Standard_Chinese" title="Standard Chinese">Mandarin Chinese</a> film adaptation of the series, <i><a href="/wiki/Dragon_Ball:_The_Magic_Begins" title="Dragon Ball: The Magic Begins">Dragon Ball: The Magic Begins</a></i>, was released in <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a> in 1989.<sup id="cite_ref-AnimeEncyc_7-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AnimeEncyc-7">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> In December 1990, the unofficial live-action Korean film <i><a href="/wiki/Dragon_Ball:_Ssawora_Son_Goku,_Igyeora_Son_Goku" title="Dragon Ball: Ssawora Son Goku, Igyeora Son Goku">Dragon Ball: Ssawora Son Goku, Igyeora Son Goku</a></i> was released.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/The_Matrix_(franchise)" title="The Matrix (franchise)"><i>The Matrix</i> franchise</a> echoes <i>Dragon Ball Z</i> in several action scenes, including the climactic fights of the 2003 films <i><a href="/wiki/Matrix_Reloaded" class="mw-redirect" title="Matrix Reloaded">Matrix Reloaded</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Matrix_Revolutions" class="mw-redirect" title="Matrix Revolutions">Matrix Revolutions</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup> Filino-American film storyboard artist <a href="/wiki/Jay_Oliva" title="Jay Oliva">Jay Oliva</a> has cited <i>Dragon Ball</i> as a major inspiration on his work, particularly the action scenes of 2013 <a href="/wiki/Superman_film" class="mw-redirect" title="Superman film">Superman film</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Man_of_Steel_(film)" title="Man of Steel (film)">Man of Steel</a></i>, which launched the <a href="/wiki/DC_Extended_Universe" title="DC Extended Universe">DC Extended Universe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup> Several films in the <a href="/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe" title="Marvel Cinematic Universe">Marvel Cinematic Universe</a> have also been visually influenced by <i>Dragon Ball Z</i>. <a href="/wiki/Erik_Killmonger" title="Erik Killmonger">Erik Killmonger</a>'s battle armour in <i><a href="/wiki/Black_Panther_(film)" title="Black Panther (film)">Black Panther</a></i> (2018) bears a resemblance to Vegeta's battle armour,<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup> which actor <a href="/wiki/Michael_B._Jordan" title="Michael B. Jordan">Michael B. Jordan</a> (himself a <i>Dragon Ball</i> fan) said may have inspired Killmonger's battle armor.<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup> The fiery look of <a href="/wiki/Carol_Danvers" title="Carol Danvers">Carol Danvers</a>' Binary powers in <i><a href="/wiki/Captain_Marvel_(film)" title="Captain Marvel (film)">Captain Marvel</a></i> (2019) also drew some influence from <i>Dragon Ball Z</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_and_sports">Music and sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dragon_Ball&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Music and sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>Dragon Ball</i> has been channeled and referenced by numerous musicians. It is popular in the <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop" title="Hip hop">hip hop</a> community, and has been referenced in numerous <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">hip hop songs</a> by rappers and artists such as <a href="/wiki/Chris_Brown" title="Chris Brown">Chris Brown</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chance_the_Rapper" title="Chance the Rapper">Chance the Rapper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Big_Sean" title="Big Sean">Big Sean</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lil_Uzi_Vert" title="Lil Uzi Vert">Lil Uzi Vert</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=G-Mo_Skee&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="G-Mo Skee (page does not exist)">G-Mo Skee</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Weeknd" title="The Weeknd">The Weeknd</a>, <a href="/wiki/Childish_Gambino" class="mw-redirect" title="Childish Gambino">Childish Gambino</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-cleveland_220-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cleveland-220">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/B.o.B" class="mw-redirect" title="B.o.B">B.o.B</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soulja_Boy" title="Soulja Boy">Soulja Boy</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Drake_(rapper)" class="mw-redirect" title="Drake (rapper)">Drake</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Frank_Ocean" title="Frank Ocean">Frank Ocean</a>, and Sese.<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Numerous athletes have also channeled and referenced <i>Dragon Ball</i>, including <a href="/wiki/NBA" class="mw-redirect" title="NBA">NBA</a> <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a> players such as <a href="/wiki/Sacramento_Kings" title="Sacramento Kings">Sacramento Kings</a> guard <a href="/wiki/De%27Aaron_Fox" title="De&#39;Aaron Fox">De'Aaron Fox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Bulls" title="Chicago Bulls">Chicago Bulls</a> forward <a href="/wiki/Lauri_Markkanen" title="Lauri Markkanen">Lauri Markkanen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Golden_State_Warriors" title="Golden State Warriors">Golden State Warriors</a> player <a href="/wiki/Jordan_Bell" title="Jordan Bell">Jordan Bell</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers" title="Los Angeles Lakers">Los Angeles Lakers</a> guard <a href="/wiki/Lonzo_Ball" title="Lonzo Ball">Lonzo Ball</a>, <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">American football</a> <a href="/wiki/NFL" class="mw-redirect" title="NFL">NFL</a> stars such as <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Browns" title="Cleveland Browns">Cleveland Browns</a> players <a href="/wiki/Darren_Fells" title="Darren Fells">Darren Fells</a> and <a href="/wiki/David_Njoku" title="David Njoku">David Njoku</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mixed_martial_artist" class="mw-redirect" title="Mixed martial artist">mixed martial artist</a> <a href="/wiki/Ronda_Rousey" title="Ronda Rousey">Ronda Rousey</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-cleveland_220-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cleveland-220">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/WWE" title="WWE">WWE</a> wrestlers such as <a href="/wiki/The_New_Day_(wrestling)" class="mw-redirect" title="The New Day (wrestling)">The New Day</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup> Additionally, Canadian mixed martial artist <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Newton" title="Carlos Newton">Carlos Newton</a> dubbed his fighting style "Dragon Ball <a href="/wiki/Jiu-Jitsu" class="mw-redirect" title="Jiu-Jitsu">Jiu-Jitsu</a>" in tribute to the series.<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup> Other mixed martial artists inspired by <i>Dragon Ball</i> include <a href="/wiki/Yushin_Okami" title="Yushin Okami">Yushin Okami</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yoshihiro_Akiyama" title="Yoshihiro Akiyama">Yoshihiro Akiyama</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yuya_Wakamatsu" title="Yuya Wakamatsu">Yuya Wakamatsu</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Video_games_2">Video games</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dragon_Ball&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Video games">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The producer of the <i><a href="/wiki/Tekken" title="Tekken">Tekken</a></i> video game series, <a href="/wiki/Katsuhiro_Harada" title="Katsuhiro Harada">Katsuhiro Harada</a>, said that <i>Dragon Ball</i> was one of the first works to visually depict <a href="/wiki/Qi" title="Qi">chi</a> and thereby influenced numerous <a href="/wiki/Japanese_video_games" class="mw-redirect" title="Japanese video games">Japanese video games</a>, especially <a href="/wiki/Fighting_games" class="mw-redirect" title="Fighting games">fighting games</a> such as <i>Tekken</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Street_Fighter" title="Street Fighter">Street Fighter</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-GI_247-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GI-247">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup> Masaaki Ishikawa, art director of the video game <i><a href="/wiki/Arms_(video_game)" title="Arms (video game)">Arms</a></i>, said that its art style was largely influenced by <i>Dragon Ball</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Akira_(manga)" title="Akira (manga)">Akira</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup> French video game designer <a href="/wiki/%C3%89ric_Chahi" title="Éric Chahi">Éric Chahi</a> also cited <i>Dragon Ball</i> as an influence on his 1991 <a href="/wiki/Cinematic_platformer" class="mw-redirect" title="Cinematic platformer">cinematic platformer</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Another_World_(video_game)" title="Another World (video game)">Another World</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Eric_Chahi_Interview_249-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eric_Chahi_Interview-249">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup> Other <a href="/wiki/Video_game_industry" title="Video game industry">video game industry</a> veterans who were inspired by <i>Dragon Ball</i> include <a href="/wiki/Suda51" class="mw-redirect" title="Suda51">Suda51</a>, <a href="/wiki/SWERY" class="mw-redirect" title="SWERY">SWERY</a>, <a href="/wiki/Insomniac_Games" title="Insomniac Games">Insomniac Games</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nina_Freeman" title="Nina Freeman">Nina Freeman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heart_Machine" title="Heart Machine">Heart Machine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iron_Galaxy" title="Iron Galaxy">Iron Galaxy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mega64" title="Mega64">Mega64</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-GI_247-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GI-247">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

</li>

<li id="cite_note-204"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-204">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><i>Dragon Ball</i> toys and merchandise are also manufactured and distributed by other companies. <a href="/wiki/List_of_Dragon_Ball_video_games" title="List of Dragon Ball video games"><i>Dragon Ball</i> video games</a> were also published by <a href="/wiki/Atari,_Inc._(Atari,_SA_subsidiary)" class="mw-redirect" title="Atari, Inc. (Atari, SA subsidiary)">Atari</a> in North America.</span>
